Cost = (100 km / 20 km/l) * â‚¹100/l + â‚¹50

[23/08/23, 8:10:21â€¯PM] ThiyagaB: A space agency is planning to send a satellite from Earth to the Moon using a Hohmann transfer orbit. The details are as follows:

The distance from the Earth's surface to the satellite's initial orbit is 300 km.
The average distance from the Earth's surface to the Moon is 384,100 km.
The Hohmann transfer orbit is an elliptical path. One end (closest point to Earth) starts at the satellite's initial orbit, and the other end (farthest point from Earth) touches the Moon's orbit.

Calculate:

a) The distance from Earth's center to the satellite's initial orbit.
b) The distance from Earth's center to the Moon.
c) The average distance (or semi-major axis) of the Hohmann transfer orbit.

[23/08/23, 8:26:52â€¯PM] ~â€¯~TheDiabloğŸ˜ˆ~: a)6,371 km + 300 km = 6,671 km

b)384,100 km + 6,371 km = 390,471 km

c) The average distance (or semi-major axis) of the Hohmann transfer orbit can be calculated using the following formula:

a = (r1 + r2)/2 + (r2 - r1)/2 * sqrt(2)

Where:
a = semi-major axis
r1 = distance from Earth's center to the satellite's initial orbit
r2 = distance from Earth's center to the Moon

a = (6,671 km + 390,471 km)/2 + (390,471 km - 6,671 km)/2 * sqrt(2)
a = 198,571 km

[26/08/23, 8:54:47â€¯PM] ~â€¯shriram: Game: Inside 
Reason: The protagonist of the game is a little boy whose shoes we control. The game set in a dystopian world where human beingsÂ  are being trafficked, harnessed for their energy and used as lab rats. The game starts with the little boy escaping the facility where all other humans are being held captives. He is soon noticed by those in control of the facility. Our objective as players is to lead the little boy away from the unknown force and away from danger to a safe place. The game is a typical sidescroller with 2dimensional movements. It is a short game with 17 or so hand crafted levels. These levels mostly require us to solve some puzzles to get through them. Throughout these levels we encounter various horrors of the facility and and we must find innovative ways to manipulate our environment. There are a few aspects of this game which in my opinion makes it one of the more interesting games I've played this year. For starters the entire game is monochromatic. Yes, just black and white. Now, one might think that'll only make the game boring. But hell nah, it sets the mood for the dystopian environment I described before. And the sound design is just chefs kiss. It's subtle but not unnoticeable. It's adds so much depth to the game whilst also not interfering with the gameplay itself. Another interesting aspect Is that the game contains no dialogue. Literally 0. How does one convey the story and the setting without dialogues, one might wonder. That's where the atmospheric design of the game and the sound design and the monochromaticity of the game comes into play. The developer has found a brilliant way to convey raw emotions through just the atmosphere and sound, nothing else. What sort of enjoyment does the player get from these kinda games? The answer is, experience. This game will make you think about it, wonder about it for hours after competing it. It offers an unparalleled gameplay experience. Undoubtedly the game is dark. But the story is just so unique and fascinating at some points. The puzzles are fairly intermediate. Nothing too difficult. One of the most important aspect is that Throughout the game we are led to believe that the entire game revolves around us just like any other game. But as we reach the end, weÂ  come to a realisation that we do not occupy a center stage. We are just like everybody else in the game ie nobody. We realise that the entire plot was preplanned, staged by the unknown force just as an experiment(a cruel one at that). 
To conclude, I think this game offers a satirical take on modern society. Whether this take holds good or not remains open to discussion. :)

[27/08/23, 12:24:56â€¯PM] ~â€¯Salai Kowshikan: *Sans predire (translates to â€œThe inability to predictâ€)*

Chess is a fairly simple game with rules set in stone. So what if the rules of chess becomes randomized for the each game?  With  even more randomness than the Fischer chess. 

*Mechanics:*

Each match would be a regular game of chess but three modifiers (from a vast pool of pre written modifiers) will be chosen at random. _some examples for modifiers are as follows:_

- _Killing the queen ends the game_
- _The knight can move up to 8 tiles as long as the path makes an L shape_
- _Rooks can't move for more than 3 tiles but now it can leap over other units_
- _When a player has done twenty moves, they may choose to revive one of their pieces and place them back into the game at the starting position. They need to do this in their turn before making a move and this will consume their entire turn, ending it instantly._
- _Pawns get +1 range.(they can move an additional tile)_

And so on. Each game will have different modifiers (randomized), leading to variance in each of the games played. The modifier pool will be large enough for it (say around 32)

Since the modifiers are applied to both the players, it will be balanced and fair. Two modes will be provided - casual with no care for winning or losing and ranked where elo rating comes into consideration.
[27/08/23, 12:25:28â€¯PM] ~â€¯Salai Kowshikan: *Player retention:*

This will be a live service game so player retention will be a huge determining factor for the success. This part can be brainstormed even more but the few things I came up with are Seasons and cosmetics.

We can have limited time ranked seasons at the end of which the elo will be reset. This way players won't be struck in the same rating and will be able to try again during the start of each season. Each season may also come with their own modifiers that are unique to them and will only be available for that season.

This game will be free to play and the main source of revenue will be cosmetics. There will be themed chessboards and pieces which also comes with their own ambient soundtracks (inspired from the board skins of legends of runeterra).
[27/08/23, 12:26:05â€¯PM] ~â€¯Salai Kowshikan: *Other modes: Blitz mode:*

The aim of the casual and ranked mode is to be balanced, fair for both side of the players. That's why the modifiers were limited to three. However, the blitz mode will be a chaotic mess. The game starts as a regular game of chess but after every eight sets of moves, a new modifier will be applied. To prevent unfair checkmates, the modifier to be applied will be shown in the side of the screen.

â€œX modifier will be applied in 7 turnsâ€

â€œX modifier will be applied in the next turnâ€

Once it's applied, a new modifier will pop up

â€œY modifier will be applied in 8 turnsâ€ 

And it will keep on going. This mode is just a breath of fresh air from the regular game mode.

[27/08/23, 1:55:43â€¯PM] ~â€¯SRI DHARANI: #1000 puzzles

A multiplayer game where you and another opponent face off in a series of puzzles and minigames. The basic working of the game is as follows - the gameplay environment are rooms - each room will have a puzzle/minigame in it and three doors. Each door will have a symbol carved on it and only one of them will get you to the next stage. Choosing a wrong door will result in a game over and the opponent will win.

At the start of the game, you and your opponent will have to go through the puzzle/minigame. Whoever wins it gets an obvious clue to the correct door letting them go to the next level while the one who lost will have to randomly guess the the door. Choosing the wrong door will result in your opponent winning the game and you will have to start from scratch. If both players chose the right door, they will be teleported to the next room with another puzzle/minigame and the gameplay goes on a loop. 

Coins will be rewarded when you select the right door which can be used to get the clue later when you lose. This prevents a player from losing suddenly after winning a lot of rounds consecutively.

[27/08/23, 4:14:00â€¯PM] Koushik PEC: "Project TN " is a vibrant and engaging city builder game set in the beautiful state of Tamil Nadu, India. Players will embark on a journey to create and manage their own virtual city, blending modern urban development with the rich cultural heritage of Tamil Nadu. The goal is to build a thriving city that celebrates the state's traditions, history, and architecture while also embracing technological advancements.

1.Cultural Diversity: Players can construct various iconic landmarks inspired by Tamil Nadu's heritage, such as intricately designed temples, classical music and dance academies, traditional marketplaces, and historical monuments.

2.Architectural Fusion: The game allows players to blend traditional South Indian architectural styles with modern infrastructure, creating a unique visual representation of a harmonious coexistence between the past and the future.

3.Festivals and Events: Incorporate major Tamil festivals like Pongal, Deepavali, and Tamil New Year, organizing in-game events that engage citizens and celebrate cultural practices, offering rewards for participation.

4.Trade and Commerce: Emphasize the historical importance of trade in Tamil Nadu by creating trade routes, spice markets, and ports for exporting goods. This adds an economic dimension to the gameplay.

5.Cultural Technologies: Research and develop technological advancements that are in harmony with Tamil Nadu's cultural identity, such as eco-friendly architecture, sustainable farming methods, and renewable energy sources.

6.Storytelling Quests: Introduce narrative-driven quests that immerse players in the history, folklore, and mythology of Tamil Nadu, encouraging them to learn more about the region.

7.Community Participation: Implement a system where players can collaborate to build community projects, such as restoring ancient structures, establishing educational institutions, or organizing cultural events.

8.Dynamic Seasons: Reflect Tamil Nadu's climate and seasons, impacting agriculture, tourism, and citizens' activities, and encouraging players to adapt their city management strategies accordingly.

9.Customizable Avatars: Allow players to create avatars that represent them within the game, dressing them in traditional attire or modern clothing, and showcasing their individuality.

10.Multiplayer Interaction: Enable players to visit and explore each other's cities, trade resources, and share cultural knowledge, fostering a sense of community and friendly competition.

"Project TN" aims to provide an engaging and educational experience while highlighting the rich heritage of Tamil Nadu. The game encourages players to appreciate the beauty of cultural integration and sustainable urban development, making it a fun and enlightening city builder game for players of all ages.

[27/08/23, 7:14:56â€¯PM] ~â€¯shriram: Name: Yet to be decided

Setting: The game is set in the year 30th century, by which point the entire planet has been taken over by superior androids. Most of the human population has relocated to Kepler452b. The people left on earth live their lives in the shadows, staying out of sight.

Story: The player controls a Paranoid Android, which is extremely fascinated by human beings. It absolutely disgusts the Fake Plastic Trees of its homeland and it strongly believes that its home lies in Kepler 452b along with the humans. An opportunity to escape presents itself when, the android comes to know of a certain shuttle leaving for Kepler in a few days. It comes up with a plan which invloves the android taking the underground tunnel system. The tunnel system consists of 17 major sections which must be traversed. These sections are heavily guarded.

Gameplay: The main weapon, the players possess in their arsenal is a device which can change the magnitude and direction of the "local" gravity. The game consists of 17 levels, each of which is filled with traps, mazes, puzzles, and armed guards. the players must find innovative ways to to traverse this deadly environment with the gravity device. Slight changes in gravity would lead to distortion in the motion of prejectiles like bullets, while significant changes could result in changes in the movements of the androids themselves, The players are also given an option of completely switching the direction of gravity. For example, projectiles from guards could be avoided by not so sognificant changes to the "local" gravity, while sabotaging a huge death laser would require the players to completely switch the direction of gravity. The players are encouraged to use the objects present to find creative ways to overcome the challenges they are presented with. Huge chasms could be crossed by changing the gravity so much that it causes the androids to float in space. The players could also opt to use zero gravity which makes traversal easier, the caveat being, this ability could be used only once per level and the players should also keep in mind that this exponentially increases the accuracy of the fired projectiles as they woudl travel in a linear path in the absence of gravity. All these levels, if completed, would make sense in the end like a Jigsaw Falling Into Place.

Goal: The players are tasked with helping the android overcome the tunnel system and reach the space shuttle(as if it isnt obvious by now lol).

*Game Concept:*
This game bridges the gap between player emotions and in-game mechanics. The game utilizes advanced voice and facial recognition technology to detect the player's real-time emotional state, translating it into unique abilities for the in-game character.

*Gameplay Mechanics:*

This game uses voice recognition and camera-based facial analysis to identify the player's emotions. This can include a range of emotions like happiness, anger, sadness, etc.
Each emotion is assigned to a set of unique in-game abilities. 
There will be certain levels that can be cleared based on the emotions we show.
This game can be interesting to play as well as make us control and analyze our emotions, which can help us in any state of reality.
The player's emotional state also influences how NPCs and creatures react. Being angry might intimidate enemies, while being happy could lead to cooperative interactions.
*Story-play:*
The game revolves around a character who gains access to a mystical world where emotions hold the key to unlocking its secrets. The character's journey would involve navigating through different emotional realms, each with its own unique challenges and puzzles.
This helps in building a powerful connection between the player's emotions and character.

*Note:*
Can be multiplayer or stand-alone gameplay

[28/08/23, 8:15:30â€¯PM] ~â€¯Vaishu: Let's assume a regular-sized Chicken Biryani can contain 700 calories.
On average, a full omelette may contain around 300-400 calories. Let's assume it's 350 calories.
A 350 ml can of regular Pepsi contains approximately 150 calories.

So,
Total Calories = Chicken Biryani (700 calories) + Omelette (350 calories) + Pepsi (150 calories) = 1200 calories

To maintain our current weight and not add any extra calories to our body, we'll need to burn these 1200 calories through physical activity, such as walking. The number of steps required to burn calories through walking can vary depending on our weight, walking speed, and other factors. On average, a person burns about 100 calories by walking approximately 1 mile (1.6 kilometers).

Assuming an average walking speed of about 3 miles per hour (4.8 kilometers per hour), you can use the following estimate:

Number of Steps = (Calories Burned / Calories Burned per Mile) x 2,000

Number of Steps = (1200 / 100) x 2,000 = 24,000 steps

So, we would need to walk approximately 24,000 steps to burn the equivalent calories from your meal and not add any extra calories to our body by the end of the day.

[04/09/23, 8:15:03â€¯PM] ~â€¯srini: If we consider the chessboard to be a boolean matrix represented by:

{
0 - Untouched by the Rook
1- The Rook has been here atleast once }

Then considering a smaller model of 2x2 boxes, at the intial position we get:
{ 0, 0
  1, 0 }

And it takes exactly one move to turn the 0s to 1s which results in 3 moves and since we have to end at the same spot we get an additional move which results in the answer n^2 where n represents either the row or column of the matrix.

Extending this to an 8x8 matrix (chesboard) we get the answer as 64

[04/09/23, 8:33:14â€¯PM] ~â€¯ğŸ¤¹â€â™‚ï¸ê§PÒ‰rÒ‰aÒ‰nÒ‰aÒ‰vÒ‰ê§vikramanê§‚ğŸ¤¿: Now i guess it can also be done by 14 moves 
After reaching the last square in the eighth row, the rook will have covered all 64 squares. Now, it can return to its starting position by moving directly back in the same path it used before, which requires 7 moves.

So, the total number of moves is 7 (covering the board) + 7 (returning to the starting position) = 14 moves.

[05/09/23, 9:34:20â€¯PM] ~â€¯N G K: Chennai is also known as Indiaâ€™s chess capital as it gave the country its forebearers of international chess. Indiaâ€™s first International Master Manuel Aaron and first GrandMaster Viswanathan Anand are from Chennai.Indiaâ€™s first Women GrandMaster (WGM), Subbaraman Vijayalakshmi is also from Tamil Nadu.

Chess clubs:
From a chess club that was formed in the early 1960s to very active district and state chess federations, we have a chess culture in the state. Even the Indian Chess Federation was based in Chennai for a very long time in initial years.One of the first well-known clubs in Chennai was started in 1972 by Manuel Aaron, who dominated chess in India from the 1960s to 1980s. The monthly membership fee was just 20 rupees.The Tal  chess Club created the cityâ€™s first chess revolution, resulting in the emergence of Anand and numerous other players in the 90s.the Velammal Vidyalaya in Mogappair is the next revolutionary chess club.  Since the beginning of 2005 ,15  grandmasters are from Velammal.

Ancient history:
There are claims that chess, known as 'Sathurangam' in the Tamil, could have originated in Tamil Nadu. The ancient 'Sathuranga Vallabhanathar' temple at Tiruvarur  is a proof.

In conclusion, Tamil Nadu has a strong chess culture with a rich history of chess players and enthusiasts. Chess is widely taught and promoted in schools.The success of chess players like Viswanathan Anand has inspired many youngsters in the state to take up chess seriously.Parents also give their support.

And humans especially have knowledge that gets passed on beyond generations other than through genetics by something called culture. This is an extremely powerful tool as the only thing that a living thing is concerned with seems to be the survival of its kind and so will be willing to do anything to achieve that and that thing is generally termed intelligence. So when we see something that we know is going to make us live longer or help us reproduce, it checks in for things necessary to survive by our genetic material whose only purpose is to continue existing. So, we tend to do such things and keep it in higher regard. For example, ancient humans saw forest fire and how animals that got cooked in them tasted and how they were better because they won't cause much diseases as the bacteria will be destroyed by heat and that became an incentive to learn how to create a fire, similarly with other things, everything just ensures one's survival. [07/09/23, 8:32:16â€¯PM] Koushik PEC: Today's question is again a open ended question,

Nowadays majority of the population has access to internet , people can conduct researches by the comfort of their home instead of depending on labs completely .

Should research papers be freely accessible to the public, or is it reasonable to require subscriptions to access them, considering the widespread availability of the internet and the evolving landscape of academic publishing?
[07/09/23, 8:35:15â€¯PM] ThiyagaB: PEC opening eh research, scientist range ku poitangale..  :).
[07/09/23, 8:36:05â€¯PM] ~â€¯Nithish: I have two different views on this...

1st:
I have published one research paper and from my experience, research papers should be opensource because, while working i myself have 
referred similar past works and ive referred to original papers about algorithms that i used in the research, also papers provide some extra information than other tutorials, and while being freely accessible it can used by anyone getting started and public benifit is there.
Also, if your work is good enough, you might get internation collaboration.

2nd:
The amount of time spent by me brainstroming on each step of research is be invaluable(from my POV), and also getting the article published required a lot of work, like when you submit to a journal they won't straight away publish it, they will look for errors, you have to correct and submit again, then for publishing also you have to pay certain amount based on the journal(I paid $150). But, that is what keeps the journal running, without the fees journals might struggle to survive. And the fees is also used as way to pay the reviewers who are reviewing your papers which is (Quality Control). Finally, the freely accessible research might lead to the exploitation of researchers, as certain entities could use their work without compensation.

In conclusion, the question of whether research papers should be freely accessible or require subscriptions is a nuanced one.

[07/09/23, 8:52:53â€¯PM] ~â€¯Salai Kowshikan: In an idealistic world, knowledge should be free for all. But as the answers before mentioned, the reviewing and quality control is very important. [08/09/23, 9:59:39â€¯PM] ~â€¯Dharun: you can calculate the number of distinct ways using permutations. 

There are 5 candidates, so for the first place, any of the 5 candidates can be chosen. Afterward, for the second place, there are 4 remaining choices, then 3 for the third place, 2 for the fourth place, and the last candidate will be in the fifth place

So, the number of distinct ways to express their preferences is:
5 (choices for 1st place) Ã— 4 (choices for 2nd place) Ã— 3 (choices for 3rd place) Ã— 2 (choices for 4th place) Ã— 1 (choice for 5th place) = 5! = 120 distinct ways.

There are 120 distinct ways for the 500 voters to express their preference

[11/09/23, 9:26:10â€¯PM] ~â€¯Gautham: Imagine a processor is like a chef in a kitchen, and it has to cook multiple dishes at once. Threading is like the chef having more than one pair of hands, so they can work on different dishes at the same time. It makes the cooking process faster and more efficient. Hyper-threading is like giving the chef even more pairs of hands, so they can do even more things at once, making the cooking (or processing) even faster

[11/09/23, 9:29:41â€¯PM] ~â€¯Chokkalingam ğŸ’›: Lets take a example of having toy car In hand
Assume you are having 1 car
You can hold it in 1 hand
What if u got 2 toy car
U would hold it in 2 hands 
Each one in one hand...

Even you own both the toy car
U r representing it showing it as
Each car in each hand

Exactly how this works..
When a computer is assigned with multiple tasks
Each task is represented as thread
Thread would look like thin small peice of whole cloth

As a saree is made of every thread in it
A process a task is made up of every small process called thread

Example you are watching a video in yt
The audio function
The command writing function

[13/09/23, 9:09:23â€¯PM] ~â€¯CR7 GAMING YT - à®¤à®®à®¿à®´à¯: Start with both jugs empty.
Fill the 3-liter jug to the top.
Pour the water from the 3-liter jug into the 5-liter jug. Now, the 3-liter jug is empty, and the 5-liter jug has 3 liters of water in it.

Now, empty the 5-liter jug completely.
Pour the 1 liter of water from the 3-liter jug into the 5-liter jug.
Finally, fill the 3-liter jug to the top and pour it into the 5-liter jug. This will fill the 5-liter jug to its maximum capacity, leaving you with exactly 4 liters of water in the 5-liter jug.

[16/09/23, 9:06:48â€¯PM] ~â€¯Aakash: THE PROBLEM STEPS :

1. Let's denote the daughter's current age as `D` and the mother's current age as M.
2. From the problem, we know that the sum of their ages is 56. So, we can write this as an equation: D + M = 56.
3. We also know that in four years, the mother's age will be three times the daughter's age. So, we can write another equation: M + 4 = 3 * (D + 4).
4. Now we have a system of two equations, and we can solve it.

By solving these equations, we find that the daughter is 12 years old and the mother is 44 years old.

[17/09/23, 9:55:47â€¯PM] ~â€¯VIGNESHWARAN: A maze path refers to finding a way through a complex, puzzle-like structure known as a maze. It's like solving a labyrinth or a puzzle where you start at one point and aim to reach another while navigating through a network of walls or obstacles. This task involves using various strategies or algorithms, like trying different paths, marking visited areas, and backtracking, to ultimately find a route from the starting point to the destination, which might not be obvious at first glance. Maze path-solving is a common problem in computer science and puzzles, often used to demonstrate and practice problem-solving techniques and algorithms.

It is used in 

-representation
-efficient exploration of elements
-memory optimisation
-finding paths

In essence, data structures provide the framework for algorithms to process and make sense of maze data, ultimately helping you navigate from the entrance to the exit efficiently. They are fundamental tools in computer science and enable solutions to a wide range of problems, not just maze pathfinding.

Output Format:

Numbers divisible by X from N to M, with each number separated by a space.

Boundary Conditions:

1 <= M <= 9999999

M <N <= 9999999

1 <= X <= 9999

Input:

2

40

7

35 28 21 14 7

[20/09/23, 9:01:11â€¯PM] ~â€¯Dharshuu: We had some great responses....though a simple sort of explanation here...
*Docker and Kubernetes*
Basically, Docker and Kubernetes are one of the most popular DevOps tools.
In simple words, Docker is a container where you can run your application without worrying about hardware and operating system versions, which makes it easy to spin off a new environment without worrying about config details.
And..
Kubernetes is that manages your container effectively.Kubernetes is the most crucial container management technology in the world and is used a lot in a real production environment where you have many containers to manage.
[20/09/23, 9:03:55â€¯PM] ThiyagaB: Nice... one bonus trivia..  
Those who feel programming eh enaku varala nu, 
There is a role in IT called 'DevOps' or 'Infra', a knowledge of Docker, Kubernetes will help you get the job, the role will have less programming and more of administration and setup.

[20/09/23, 9:33:55â€¯PM] ~â€¯Shankar Sai: "What are the main differences between the Docker Swarm and Kubernetes?
Docker Swarm is Dockerâ€™s native, open-source container orchestration platform that is used to cluster and schedule Docker containers. Swarm differs from Kubernetes in the following ways:

Docker Swarm is more convenient to set up but doesnâ€™t have a robust cluster, while Kubernetes is more complicated to set up but the benefit of having the assurance of a robust cluster
Docker Swarm canâ€™t do auto-scaling (as can Kubernetes); however, Docker scaling is five times faster than KubernetesÂ 
Docker Swarm doesnâ€™t have a GUI; Kubernetes has a GUI in the form of a dashboardÂ

[22/09/23, 9:24:09â€¯PM] ~â€¯Pranesh: Arithmetic Progression:
First term = 10
Common difference = 4
a1 = 10
So 10,14,18
Geometric progression:starts from 18
First term G1= 18
Common ratio = 2
So
G1*2=36,
G1*4=72,
G1*8=144,
Series is :
10,14,18,36,72,144
So, the sixth term of the sequence is 144.
[22/09/23, 9:25:11â€¯PM] ~â€¯Dharshuu: Yeah!!it's correct!!..
[22/09/23, 9:25:31â€¯PM] ~â€¯ğŸ‘©ğŸ»â€ğŸ“SreeğŸ‘©ğŸ»â€ğŸ“: Arithmetic Progression:
First term = 10
Common difference = 4
a1 = 10
a2 = a1 + d = 10 + 4 = 14
a3 = a2 + d = 14 + 4 = 18
Geometric progression:
First term = 18
Common ratio = 2
a4= a3 * r = 18 * 2 = 36
a5 = a4* r = 36 * 2 = 72
a6 = a5* r = 72 * 2 = 144
So, the sixth term of the sequence is 144.

def calculate_average(numbers):
    total = 0
    for num in numbers:
        total += num
    average = total / len(numbers)
    return average

result = calculate_average(numbers)
print("The average is: " result)
Options:

A) Missing a colon at the end of the for loop.
B) Using a comma instead of a plus sign to concatenate the strings.
C) Typo in the print statement, missing a comma after "average is."
D) Incorrect indentation in the for loop.

What's the correct answer (A, B, C, or D)?

[24/09/23, 9:14:34â€¯PM] ~â€¯ğŸ¤¹â€â™‚ï¸ê§PÒ‰rÒ‰aÒ‰nÒ‰aÒ‰vÒ‰ê§vikramanê§‚ğŸ¤¿: And here are some *BOOK RECOMMENDATIONS*                                                                                                            General Engineering and Inspiration:

"The Innovators" by Walter Isaacson: This book explores the history of innovation in technology and the people behind it, from Ada Lovelace to Steve Jobs.

"The Soul of a New Machine" by Tracy Kidder: A classic that delves into the world of computer engineering and the creation of a new computer.

"Structures: Or Why Things Don't Fall Down" by J.E. Gordon: A fascinating exploration of the principles of structural engineering and materials.

"To Engineer Is Human: The Role of Failure in Successful Design" by Henry Petroski: Examines how engineering often involves learning from failures and mistakes.

*Civil Engineering:*

"Civil Engineering Reference Manual" by Michael R. Lindeburg: A comprehensive reference for civil engineering students preparing for exams or looking to deepen their knowledge.

"Structural Analysis" by Russell C. Hibbeler: A textbook that covers the fundamental principles of structural analysis.

*Mechanical Engineering:*

"Shigley's Mechanical Engineering Design" by Richard G. Budynas and Keith J. Nisbett: A widely used textbook for mechanical engineering design.

"Machine Design" by Robert L. Norton: Covers the design of mechanical systems and is used in many engineering programs.

*Electrical and Electronics Engineering:*

"Microelectronic Circuits" by Adel S. Sedra and Kenneth C. Smith: An essential textbook for understanding microelectronics and integrated circuits.

"The Art of Electronics" by Paul Horowitz and Winfield Hill: A highly regarded book for electronics enthusiasts, covering both theory and practical aspects.

*Computer Science and Programming:*

"Introduction to the Theory of Computation" by Michael Sipser: Offers a deep dive into the theory of computation, a crucial topic in computer science.

"Clean Code: A Handbook of Agile Software Craftsmanship" by Robert C. Martin: Focuses on writing clean, maintainable code, a valuable skill for software engineers.                                                                                               *Self-Building and Personal Development:*

"The 7 Habits of Highly Effective People" by Stephen R. Covey: This classic book provides a framework for personal and professional effectiveness based on timeless principles.

"Atomic Habits" by James Clear: A book that explores the science of habit formation and how small changes can lead to remarkable results.

"Awaken the Giant Within" by Tony Robbins: Tony Robbins shares strategies for taking control of your emotions, finances, relationships, and life.

"Mindset: The New Psychology of Success" by Carol S. Dweck: This book explores the concept of mindset and how having a growth mindset can lead to success.

"Man's Search for Meaning" by Viktor E. Frankl: A powerful account of Viktor Frankl's experiences in a Nazi concentration camp and his exploration of the search for meaning in life.

*Inspirational Stories:*

"The Alchemist" by Paulo Coelho: A novel that follows the journey of a shepherd named Santiago as he embarks on a quest to discover his personal legend.

"The Pursuit of Happyness" by Chris Gardner: The memoir of Chris Gardner's life journey from homelessness to successful entrepreneur, also adapted into a film.

"Born a Crime: Stories from a South African Childhood" by Trevor Noah: Comedian Trevor Noah shares his remarkable and humorous life story growing up in South Africa.

"Educated" by Tara Westover: An autobiographical account of Tara Westover's journey from a strict and isolated upbringing to earning a PhD from Cambridge University.

"Wild" by Cheryl Strayed: The memoir of Cheryl Strayed's solo journey along the Pacific Crest Trail as she seeks self-discovery and healing.

[25/09/23, 10:17:11â€¯PM] ~â€¯Praveen: //valid parenthesis
#include <iostream>
using namespace std;
#include<stack>
stack<char>st;
string isvalid(string s)
{
    for(int i=0;i<s.length();i++)
    {
        st.push(s[i]);
    }
    for(int i=0;i<s.length();i++)
    {
        if(st.top()=='}')
        {
            while(!st.empty() && st.top()!='{')
            {
                st.pop();
            }
            st.pop();
        }
        else if(st.top()==']')
        {
            while(!st.empty() && st.top()!='[')
            {
                st.pop();
            }
            st.pop();
        }
        else if(st.top()==')')
        {
            while(!st.empty() && st.top()!='(')
            {
                st.pop();
            }
            st.pop();
        }
        if(st.empty())
        {
            return "Yes";
        }
        else
        {
            return "No";
        }
    }
}
int main() {
 
    string s="{()[]}";
    string res=isvalid(s);
    cout<<res;
    return 0;
}

Sixty-four players seeded from seed 1 to seed 64 participated in a knock-out tennis
tournament. Seed 1 is the highest seed and seed 64 is the lowest seed. The tournament would be played in six rounds i.e., first round, second round, third round, quarterfinals, semi finals and final. Similarly, the player with the second highest seed (i.e., 2) would play with the player with the second lowest seed (i.e., 63), which is designated Match No.2 and so on. In the second round, the winner of the Match No.1 of the first round would play with the winner of the Match No.32 of the first round and this match is designated Match No.1 of the second round.
Similarly, the winner of the Match No.2 of the first round would play with the winner of the Match No.31 of the first round and this match is designated Match No.2 of the second round and so on. In the similar pattern the subsequent rounds will be played.
If the player seeded 43 won the tournament, then which of the following players cannot be the runner-up?

3. Player seeded 46

[26/09/23, 11:05:04â€¯PM] ~â€¯MUKESH KUMAR S: Given a string S and an integer N as the input, the program must split the string into groups whose size is N and print them as the output in separate lines in a zig ag manner. If the last group size is less than N then the remaining letters must be filled with asterisk as shown in the Example Input/Output.

mput Format:

The first line contains S. The second line contains N .

Output Format:

LENGTH(S)/N+ LENGTH(S)%N lines containing the desired pattern.

Boundary Conditions

<= LENGTH(S) <= 500 2<=N<= LENGTH(S)

Example Input/Output 1: Input:

ENVIRONMENT

3 Output:

ENV

ORI

NME

Example Input/Output 2:

Input:

ENVIRONMENT

4 Output: ENVI

MINOR ENT Example Input/Output 3:

Input:

EVERYDAY

[26/09/23, 11:05:21â€¯PM] ~â€¯MUKESH KUMAR S: Inda question ku python program kedaikuma bro
[26/09/23, 11:05:34â€¯PM] ~â€¯MUKESH KUMAR S: I tried it but it is not executing
[26/09/23, 11:10:15â€¯PM] ~â€¯Gunamadhy Raja: S = input()
N = int(input())
num_lines = len(S) // N + (len(S) % N > 0)
start = 0
end = N
for i in range(num_lines):
    group = S[start:end]
    if len(group) < N:
        group += '*' * (N - len(group))
    if i % 2 == 1:
        group = group[::-1]
    print(group)
    start = end
    end += N

*Language Learning Apps:*

*Duolingo*: Duolingo is a free app that offers interactive lessons in multiple languages, including English. It covers vocabulary, grammar, and pronunciation.

*Rosetta Stone*: Rosetta Stone provides a comprehensive language learning experience. It focuses on immersion and is available as an app or online.

*Babbel*: Babbel offers courses in various languages, including English. It's known for its practical approach to language learning.

*Memrise*: Memrise uses spaced repetition to help you remember vocabulary effectively. It offers user-generated courses in many languages.

*HelloTalk*: This app connects you with native speakers for language exchange. It's a great way to practice speaking and learn from real conversations.

*Tandem*: Similar to HelloTalk, Tandem connects language learners with native speakers for language exchange and conversation practice. [30/09/23, 5:22:34â€¯PM] ~â€¯ğŸ¤¹â€â™‚ï¸ê§PÒ‰rÒ‰aÒ‰nÒ‰aÒ‰vÒ‰ê§vikramanê§‚ğŸ¤¿: Hey everyone! ğŸŒŸ I've got something important to share with you today â€“ the power of GitHub! ğŸ’¼

Imagine GitHub as your personal showcase for all your amazing projects. ğŸš€ It's not just for coders; designers and ECE students like us can benefit too! Let me explain with a real-life example:

Picture this: a regular guy uploads his project on GitHub, keeping the code secret. Later, Microsoft offers him a job! ğŸ¤¯ How cool is that? Uploading your projects on GitHub is like making yourself known to the world as a talented creator.

Now, as ECE students, we can join in too. Have you heard of domains like "Verilog"? Yep, they involve coding too! So, don't hesitate to upload your ECE projects.

Here's the trick: Make sure your projects are public, so others can see your incredible work. Worried about security? No need! GitHub is open-source, but folks can't copy your code. Plus, during interviews, your projects will shine!

In summary, GitHub is a goldmine for opportunities. It's not just about what you've done; it's about showing it to the world. Get ready to impress! ğŸ’ª

Feel free to share this with your friends, and let's unlock those GitHub benefits together! ğŸŒğŸš€


Now, let's take a closer look at the step-by-step process of how to upload your project.


1. Create a GitHub Account: ğŸš€ If you don't have one, start by signing up for a GitHub account at [github.com](https://github.com/).

2. Login to GitHub: ğŸ”‘ Log in to your GitHub account.

3. Create a New Repository: ğŸ“‚ Click on the '+' icon in the upper right corner and choose 'New repository'. Fill in the repository name, description, and other details.

4. Initialize with README: ğŸ“ You can choose to initialize the repository with a README file.

5. Add Your Project File: ğŸ“ Add your project files to a folder on your computer.

6. Open Git Bash: ğŸš If you're using Git Bash, navigate to your project folder by using the 'cd' command. 

7. Initialize Git: ğŸ”„ Type `git init` to initialize a Git repository in your project folder.

8. Add Your Files to Git: ğŸ“¤ Use `git add .` to add all your project files to the staging area. Or replace the `.` with specific file names to add them individually.

9. Commit Your Changes: ğŸ’¾ Commit your changes with `git commit -m "Initial commit"`.

10. Link to GitHub: ğŸŒ Create a connection to your GitHub repository using `git remote add origin <repository URL>`. Replace `<repository URL>` with your GitHub repository's URL.

11. Push Your Code : ğŸš€ Push your code to GitHub with `git push -u origin master`.

12. Authentication: ğŸ” GitHub will prompt you for your GitHub username and password or personal access token.

13. Check GitHub: ğŸ–¥ï¸ Visit your GitHub repository page to see your project's files.

14. Celebrate!: ğŸ‰ You've successfully uploaded your project to GitHub. Share your repository link with others.

Remember to replace `<repository URL>` and `<username>` with your actual repository URL and username. Happy coding!
